Holders of Central Temporary Vouchers Held an Inaugural Meeting Yesterday 152

Eight resolutions on implementation methods

The Joint Association of Holders of Central Bank Temporary Exchange Vouchers and National Government Ministry of Finance Treasury Bonds held an inaugural meeting yesterday afternoon and promoted Wu Deyu as the chairman. The meeting was held as scheduled. First, the chairman gave a speech, saying that the warlords Yan Feng and other reactionary forces have been wiped out, and the country is unified and the people are rejoicing. The central government is working hard to govern and renew the people. All internal and external debts are being planned and consolidated. It can be seen that the central government cares about national credit and understands the difficulties of the people. However, the Central Bank's temporary exchange vouchers were issued and circulated in the market during the military period of the Northern Expedition in the 15th year of the Republic of China. It has a completely different nature from other internal debts and must be consolidated and fully recovered as soon as possible. The National Government Ministry of Finance Treasury Bonds were issued on June 30th of the 16th year and expired on December 31st of the same year. The treasury bonds were issued by the Ministry of Finance to supplement the national treasury and regulate finance. Now that they have been overdue for three years, they should be recovered immediately to alleviate the difficulties of the people, etc. Then, everyone spoke in succession and resolved the implementation methods as follows: (1) Submit a request to National Government Chairman Chiang, Premier of the Executive Yuan, and Minister of Finance to ask them to consider the difficulties of the people and fully redeem and recover the vouchers as soon as possible. (2) Send letters to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the National Federation of Industry and Commerce, and other groups in various provinces, cities, and counties to ask them to sympathize and assist in alleviating the difficulties of businesses. (3) Appoint Wu Deyu, Pan Jiazhen, Dai Dachen, Zhou Bore, Qiu Juping, Dong Xihou, Yin Xiwu, Shao Xuelin, and Pan Bingchen as representatives of the association to be responsible for handling all internal and external matters. (4) Issue a declaration. (5) Schedule a date to go to Beijing to petition. (6) Post advertisements to notify voucher holders in other cities to join the registration. (7) Schedule a date to entertain the press. (8) Zhou Bore was commissioned to draft the presentation and letters. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Petition to the Central Government from the Jiangxi Provincial Association 157

Enumerating Six Matters

The representatives of the Jiangxi Sojourners Association in Shanghai who petitioned the Kuomintang National Government during the Fourth Plenary Session in Nanjing, presented the following petition: We humbly implore the dispatch of a high-ranking military officer to personally oversee the suppression of the communist bandits in Jiangxi Province, and present our humble views on post-disaster management to alleviate the suffering of the people. We note that the communist bandit scourge in Jiangxi has lasted for over three years, and its impact has been felt in over seventy counties. The loss of life and property is incalculable, and the dire situation has been repeatedly reported, and presumably noted by the authorities. However, in light of past failures and current shortcomings, we propose a post-disaster management plan and have publicly elected five members of our association, namely Zeng, Wu, Yun, He Erfei, Qian Pinsong, and Rao Junqi, as representatives to respectfully present our case to your esteemed departments. (1) We request that Commander-in-Chief Chiang personally oversee the bandit suppression efforts. The communist bandits in Jiangxi Province should be easily eliminated. However, due to the incompetence and negligence of the provincial authorities and military commanders, the disaster has persisted. Although additional troops have been dispatched to assist in the suppression, deep-seated problems remain. There is excessive demarcation of responsibilities, as evidenced by Commander Liu Zhi's report to Commander-in-Chief Chiang, stating that "this side and that side" cannot coordinate their suppression efforts. Therefore, despite the large concentration of troops, lost territories have not been recovered. This is why the Jiangxi sojourners in Hankou and other places have all requested that Commander-in-Chief Chiang personally oversee the suppression efforts. Our association shares the same view. Even if this request cannot be granted, we urge the swift appointment of either He, the overall commander of the Jiangxi bandit suppression, or one of the two division commanders, Liu Zhi and Xiong Shi, to be stationed in Jiangxi Province and given a deadline to eliminate the bandits. This would ensure unified command and clear accountability. (2) We request the swift implementation of an encirclement and suppression plan. Historically, the most effective method for dealing with roving bandits has been encirclement and suppression. This was the case with the suppression of bandits during the Qing Dynasty, the suppression of Bai Lang, and even the previous joint suppression of the communist bandits in Jinggangshan. Otherwise, the bandits will simply move around as the troops pursue them, wasting military resources and harming the people. The method of suppressing bandits by dividing the area is akin to treating a headache by only treating the head or pain, leading to many problems and should not be used. Only a simultaneous encirclement by Hunan, Guangdong, Fujian, and Jiangxi can ensure that there will be no day for complete eradication. (3) We request the establishment of a special supply depot to unify the provision of supplies and strictly prohibit the establishment of separate lists and arbitrary exactions. The cost of bandit suppression is undoubtedly significant. If a special supply depot is not established to unify the provision of supplies, it will be difficult to avoid situations where some units are well-supplied while others are lacking. This will fail to motivate the officers and achieve significant results. The national military expenditure is already provided by the national treasury, and there is no reason to impose additional levies on local areas outside of the allocated military budget. However, the Jiangxi provincial government constantly uses the threat of troop mutiny due to a lack of military pay as a means of coercing contributions under various pretexts. These exactions are not approved by the central government, and the people are not allowed to appeal. Moreover, the troops stationed in various areas freely extort money. Even the act of deploying troops has become a source of income. If the people request the suppression of bandits, they must pay a deployment fee. If they request that troops not be deployed, they must pay a non-deployment fee. Even if troops are deployed and the people are forced to flee with the army, they must still pay a protection fee. Other forms of extortion are commonplace. The people, already suffering from natural disasters, man-made calamities, and the oppression of capitalism, have been further devastated by communist bandit raids. They can no longer withstand such exploitation. Therefore, a strict order must be issued to prohibit troops from freely raising funds locally, as this would only create opportunities for the communist bandits. (4) We request the establishment of a post-disaster committee to supplement the government's efforts. In areas affected by communist bandits, it seems that everyone is a bandit. In reality, many are merely coerced followers. Killing them will only harden their resolve to become bandits and eliminate any hope for their rehabilitation. Moreover, what does the people's housing have to do with bandits? Destroying them will only demoralize society. Therefore, there is no need to question the authenticity of their banditry. It is only necessary to distinguish between the leaders and the followers and to differentiate between the treatment of people and property. To achieve this, it is necessary to appoint local respected gentry and virtuous party members to form a post-disaster committee to handle these matters. Otherwise, even if the bandit scourge is temporarily suppressed, military-related disasters will be difficult to avoid. (5) We request the implementation of the Baojia system to eliminate the source of bandits. The Baojia system has been abandoned and local autonomy has not been implemented, allowing the communist bandits to spread their propaganda. Now, after the bandit suppression, the military or county magistrates will enforce the clearing of the countryside, which, based on recent events in various areas, will only create opportunities for the military or county magistrates to abuse their power and extort wealth. Restoring the Baojia system, even if it does not bring great benefits, will not cause great harm. (6) We request the allocation of ten million in disaster relief bonds to aid the disaster-stricken people. The Jiangxi Province has been suffering for a long time, the affected area is vast, and the suffering is more severe than in any other province. Refugees are everywhere, waiting to be fed. Without significant relief funds, it will be difficult to alleviate their suffering. Since the central government has already ordered relief efforts for Hunan and other provinces, there should be no distinction between them. Therefore, we propose the allocation of ten million in disaster relief bonds to provide relief during the suppression efforts, and we request the reduction or exemption of land taxes, and at the very least, the elimination of exorbitant taxes and levies. The above six matters are the urgent requests of our association and the people of Jiangxi. We humbly implore your esteemed departments to understand our foolishness, sympathize with our poverty, and adopt our proposals to achieve their realization. We await your orders with utmost apprehension.

The matter has been approved by the ministry, which has consulted the Weihaiwei Reception Administration regarding the subsidy. Once the administration's response is received, the China Merchants Bureau will be notified. Therefore, the China Merchants Bureau must wait for the Weihaiwei Administration to approve the subsidy before opening the Weihaiwei shipping route.

Japanese Rice Shipped to Hankou: After a large shipment of Japanese rice arrived in Shanghai, the municipal authorities decided to prohibit rice merchants from purchasing it. The rice remains stored in Shanghai warehouses. Recently, Japanese merchants have proposed selling the rice in batches to the Yangtze River region. Shipments have already begun, with each batch consisting of four to five hundred bags, transported by Japanese ships.

Municipal Government to Survey Unauthorized Bank Construction; 163

Wusong River Dredging Unlikely This Year

During the winter season when the water level of the Suzhou Creek is low, vessels become congested, often causing blockages that hinder commercial transport. Previously, the Construction Committee, responding to requests from various parties, decided to expedite dredging to facilitate water transport. The Construction Committee organized a special committee for dredging the Wusong River, with representatives from relevant parties and the Municipal Government. After several meetings, a dredging plan was drafted, dividing the river into eight sections. Funding for the dredging would be raised by the various counties. Regarding the engineering aspects, the Dredging Bureau has sufficient personnel, equipment, and funds, so the Construction Committee and the Municipal Government will supervise the work and order the Dredging Bureau to provide detailed dredging plans and budgets for the first section of the project (from Waibaidu Bridge to Yejidun). Since then, the Dredging Bureau has been actively preparing dredging equipment, drawings, and a large dredging vessel, which has been completed. All procedures are in place, awaiting approval from the National Government before work can begin. It is now reported that the Construction Committee has been discussing the matter with key figures in the National Government, as it is difficult to raise funds for dredging the entire river and the unauthorized construction of banks and docks by foreigners along the Suzhou Creek has not been resolved. Starting work immediately may lead to many disputes over sovereignty. Therefore, the plan submitted by the Dredging Bureau has not been approved and has been effectively shelved. It is now reported that the Municipal Port Authority is negotiating with the Public Works Department regarding the unauthorized construction of banks and has requested that the Municipal Government schedule a survey. It appears that dredging the Suzhou Creek is unlikely to be realized this year.

Industry Representatives Petition to Safeguard Trade Regulations: 164

Representatives Scheduled to Return to Shanghai Today

The representatives of the Shanghai Municipal Trade Associations who were dispatched to Nanjing to petition for the implementation of trade regulations, Zheng Chengqing, Luo Qinghua, Ye Jiaxing, Sun Mingqi, Sun Choucheng, Cheng Guichu, and Yuan Hongjun, arrived at the Central Hotel in Nanjing on the morning of the 19th. At 10:00 a.m., they petitioned various government agencies, first visiting the National Government, where they were received by Secretary Zhu Wenzhong, who agreed to accept the Shanghai merchants' petition. They then visited the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, where they were received by Director Zhang Yiou, who discussed the issue of trade regulations in detail. He stated that the ministry was currently studying the matter and would submit it to the ministry's meeting for discussion. He also said that the ministry paid close attention to trade regulations and would do its best to maintain them. The representatives were satisfied and left. In the afternoon, the representatives visited Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum. It is reported that they will return to Shanghai by train today. The petition is as follows: We respectfully petition that the trade regulations passed by the National Industry and Commerce Conference, after being approved by the relevant government departments, should be uniformly observed by all members of the trade, whether or not they have joined the association, in order to maintain unity and benefit commerce. The powers granted to trade associations by the Trade Association Law promulgated by the National Government are to maintain and promote the common interests of the trade and to correct malpractices in business. The means of promoting public interest and correcting malpractices are the trade regulations formulated by the trade associations in accordance with the inherent good customs of the industry. However, these trade regulations must be observed by all members of the trade, both inside and outside the association, in order to be effective. Otherwise, members of the association will not only fulfill various social obligations but will also be subject to the trade regulations, while non-members will be able to act freely and disrupt order. Not only will non-members not want to join the association, but even members of the association will withdraw, resulting in the collapse of the association or its transformation into a mere formality. The absence of common principles in business will inevitably lead to disorganization and irreparable damage. Taking past experiences as examples, the encroachment of the silk, satin, blue cloth, foreign print, and dyeing industries on the business of the organized trade associations has rendered them mere formalities, and business disputes in the dyeing industry have increased daily with no hope of improvement. In addition, the dissolution of the phonograph case trade association due to the inability of trade regulations to bind non-members has led to the decline of a handicraft industry that imitates Western products and resists foreign goods. Furthermore, Du Rongtai's deliberate violation of the trade regulations of the Western-style flower board chair trade association, despite the government's desire to rectify the situation, has not been effectively sanctioned due to legal constraints, and remains an unresolved case. Other examples include shoddy workmanship, undermining commercial credibility, and disrupting the market, making industry improvement almost impossible. Fortunately, the National Industry and Commerce Conference has passed a resolution stating that the trade regulations, after being approved by the relevant government departments, must be uniformly observed by all members of the trade, whether or not they have joined the association. The associations should wait for the government's order and dare not make further requests. However, in view of the importance of trade regulations and the urgency of the situation, we have specially elected Qinghua, Sun Shouchang, Zheng Chengqing, Dong Jiayu, Ge Liangqing, Yuan Hongjun, Cheng Guichu, Mao Chuntuan, Zhuang Meiyun, and Sun Zhiqi as representatives to present our petition to the ministry. We humbly implore you to grant us an audience and swiftly adopt and implement our proposals in order to maintain unity and benefit commerce. We respectfully submit this petition to the Minister of Industry and Commerce Kong, from the Shanghai Municipal Coal Industry, Footwear Industry, Candle Industry, Shaoxing Wine Industry, Clothing Store Industry, Lacquer Industry, Jewelry Industry, Fur Industry, Face Powder Industry, Native Cloth Industry, Soybean and Rice Industry, Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry, Construction Factory Slow Train From Nanjing to Shanghai Derailed Last Night 165

The accident occurred between Anting and Huangdu; Night trains in both directions were stopped. Around 10:50 last night, the 20th slow train (third and fourth class) from Nanjing to Shanghai derailed four fourth-class carriages at the 26-kilometer mark between Anting and Huangdu stations. It is reported that the cause was that some unknown person had removed a section of rail and the dog spikes. Due to the darkness, it was impossible to repair the damage, resulting in the accident. Some passengers and railway staff were reportedly injured. The night train from Shanghai to Nanjing was turned back to Shanghai from Nanxiang. The North Station is currently assembling medical, engineering, and train staff to send a rescue train to the scene of the accident. Zheng Baozhao, Deputy Director of Train Operations, is also going to the scene to investigate.

Sun Weicheng, Captain of the Public Victory warship (i.e., Zodiac warship), previously took leave due to stomach cancer and was hospitalized in Shanghai. Unfortunately, his illness was incurable, and he passed away in the hospital the day before yesterday. Naval officers in Shanghai are deeply saddened.

The Municipal Finance Bureau Revises Three Sets of Regulations (Continued) 167

Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau Regulations on Penalties for Illegal Ship Operations (Article 1) These regulations are formulated in accordance with Article 11 of the Detailed Rules for the Collection of Ship Taxes. (Article 2) The ships subject to these regulations are limited to those that pay taxes to this bureau. (Article 3) Ships found to be unregistered will be fined three times the daily or per-trip tax amount in accordance with Article 6 of the Detailed Rules for Collection. (Article 4) Newly inspected and registered ships that cannot prove that they have not previously operated in the city's rivers will be fined twice the monthly or per-trip tax amount. (Article 5) Ships that are found to be registered but have not paid taxes will be required to pay the current monthly or per-trip tax and make up the unpaid taxes in accordance with Article 9 of the Detailed Rules for Ship Tax Collection, as well as pay the following fines according to their class: (A) Failure to pay taxes for one month or one trip or more will result in a fine equal to half the monthly or per-trip tax amount. (B) Failure to pay taxes for three months or three trips or more will result in a fine equal to the monthly or per-trip tax amount. (C) Failure to pay taxes for six months or six trips or more will result in a fine equal to twice the monthly or per-trip tax amount. (D) Failure to pay taxes for nine months or nine trips or more will result in a fine equal to three times the monthly or per-trip tax amount. (Explanation) For example, the monthly tax for a third-class ship on the Huangpu River is $1.25. If the tax is not paid for one to three months, in addition to paying the tax for those months, a fine equal to half the monthly tax amount, or $0.625, will be imposed. For a third-class ship on the Wusong River, the per-trip tax is $5. If the tax is not paid for one to three trips, in addition to paying the tax for those trips, a fine equal to half the per-trip tax amount, or $2.50, will be imposed. Other cases will be handled similarly. (Article 6) Any ship that falsely reports leaving the city but continues to operate in the city's rivers with the intention of evading taxes will be handled in accordance with Article 5 and will also be subject to an additional one-month fine. (Article 7) Any ship whose tax certificate number does not match the registration number of the Public Utilities Bureau or the Port Authority will be fined one month's or one trip's tax amount according to its class, and its tax certificate will be revoked. (Article 8) Anyone who violates any of the following items will be fined half of one month's or one trip's worth of taxes based on the class. (A) Failure to immediately apply for a new certificate if the tax certificate is lost. (B) Failure to properly display the tax certificate or improper display. (C) Resistance to inspection by the Bureau's inspectors. (Article 9) These penalty rules and past supplementary tax collection methods and penalty rules shall be abolished from the date that they are approved for promulgation. (Article 10) These penalty rules may be amended at any time if there are matters that are not fully addressed. (Article 11) These penalty rules shall be implemented from the date that they are approved by the Municipal Government.

Achievements of the Nanhui Cotton Experiment Station 169

The Effects of Breeding Become Apparent Amidst Reports of Crop Failures This year, the cotton harvest season suffered from more than 20 days of incessant rain in late August and early September, causing cotton bolls to rot and leading to poor harvests in most areas. It is reported that the Jiangsu Provincial Cotton Experiment Station Nanhui Branch has completed its cotton harvest, with an average yield of 140 catties of seed cotton per mu and a maximum yield of 169 catties per mu. Local farmers' best yield is only 90 catties per mu. The station's ability to achieve these results is due to careful cultivation, meticulous management, and the obvious effect of breeding. The improved white-seed cotton bred by the station has strong, robust, high-yielding, and long-staple characteristics. Among the households that received seeds this year, Cai Xueqin planted 17 mu and harvested a total of 2,044 catties of seed cotton, with an average yield of 120 catties per mu. Hong Yun of Yongding Temple planted 6 mu and averaged 119 catties per mu. Xia Jinsheng planted 10 mu and averaged 110 catties per mu, which is also better than neighboring farms. The cotton bolls on the cotton plants are visibly different from those in neighboring fields. Therefore, farmers generally feel that the station's cotton seeds are excellent and believe that the breeding is successful. In order to strictly control seed distribution, the station charges a seed price of three yuan per dan of cotton seeds. Recently, the cotton seeds have not yet been ginned, but all the cotton seeds have already been pre-ordered, which shows the farmers' deep faith in the station.

City Government Promulgates Regulations for the Management of Private Cemeteries 174

In order to promote public health, the Municipal Health Bureau formulated "Regulations for the Management of Private Cemeteries" some time ago and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval and implementation. It is understood that the Municipal Government believes that there are already many private cemeteries in the city, and their internal equipment and construction are indeed greatly related to public health. Moreover, since the regulations are based on the Cemetery Ordinance, they are necessary. The Municipal Government approved and promulgated the regulations yesterday. The regulations are transcribed below:

Shanghai Municipal Regulations for the Management of Private Cemeteries (Promulgated on November of the 19th Year) Article 1: The establishment of cemeteries in this city shall comply with the Cemetery Ordinance and these regulations. Article 2: When preparing to establish a private cemetery, the operator should first submit a detailed map of the selected location along with a detailed plan to the Health Bureau for approval, and then apply to the Public Works Bureau for a building permit before starting construction. Article 3: After obtaining a building permit, a private cemetery shall apply to the Health Bureau for registration and issuance of a license. Cemeteries established before the promulgation of these regulations shall apply for registration within two months after the promulgation of these regulations. Article 4: The land occupied by each grave in a private cemetery shall not exceed two meters in length, two meters in width, and the surrounding fence shall not exceed meters in height. The depth of each burial pit shall be at least meters, with the coffin buried at least half a meter above the ground. Article 5: The maximum land price for each grave in a private cemetery shall not exceed one hundred yuan. Article 6: Private cemeteries shall provide free burial plots, not less than one-twentieth of the number of paid burial plots. Article 7: Private cemeteries may handle coffin transportation, pit digging, tomb construction, and tombstone erection for users, but standard prices should be specified in advance, and no additional charges may be requested afterward. If the user hires workers to handle the above matters themselves, the operator shall not force the user to have the cemetery handle it, unless it obstructs the architectural style stipulated by the cemetery. Article 8: The temporary mortuary attached to a private cemetery shall not exceed three rooms, and each room shall not hold more than five coffins, and each coffin shall not be stored for more than thirty days. If the number of rooms or coffins exceeds the regulations, a fine of fifty yuan will be imposed for each room or coffin, and the excess rooms shall be demolished or altered, and the excess coffins shall be buried. Article 9: Private cemeteries shall establish a maintenance fund and must have workers specifically assigned to guard the tombs, sweep the cemetery, and cultivate flowers and plants. Article 10: The operator of a private cemetery shall number the graves and report the name, origin, age, occupation, cause of death, and burial date of the newly buried person to the Health Bureau on a monthly basis for record-keeping, and submit a complete register at the end of each year. Article 11: Private cemeteries shall be subject to the supervision of the Health Bureau and shall promptly improve matters related to health in accordance with instructions. Article 12: If a private cemetery violates the Cemetery Ordinance or these regulations, the Health Bureau shall, according to the circumstances, give a warning to the operator or responsible manager or impose a fine of up to one hundred yuan. If the violation is repeated, the license may be revoked and the operation ordered to cease. Article 13: These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation.

The Local Produce Trade Association yesterday sent a letter to the Sixth District Public Security Bureau and the Zhabei Water Patrol Team, requesting them to send police to stop the harassment of merchants by vagrants at Caojiadu, the illegal interception of goods, and forced sales. The original letter is transcribed below for your information: Respected Sirs, Our association has received reports from various members, who in turn received reports from merchants from western villages, stating that they used boats to transport goods to Shanghai, hoping to entrust them to our member firms for sale. However, when passing through Caojiadu, they were hailed by many people resembling vagrants on the shore, who ordered them to stop, or they would be hit by bricks and stones. To avoid danger, they had to stop the boats. Unexpectedly, without the consent of the owners, these vagrants forcibly unloaded the goods and sold them to firms there at arbitrary prices, regardless of the cost of the goods, and ordered the merchants to return to their villages, preventing them from reaching our member firms, resulting in significant losses. We request you to find a way to provide relief. Previously, a merchant named Gao Mingxing and others transported goods from Jiaxing to Shanghai and were forcibly intercepted and sold by biased individuals from Xinshun Firm in Caojiadu. The merchant reported the case to your bureau, and the individuals were arrested and sent to court for legal action. Merchants have the right to choose which firm to entrust with the sale of their goods. How can they be intercepted halfway? This is happening in the Chinese area. What kind of system is this? When merchants refuse to comply with their orders, they are hit by bricks and stones, endangering their lives. This is extremely dangerous. To protect merchants, we hereby request your bureau to promptly dispatch police to investigate and punish such incidents severely to deter others and reassure merchants. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Sixth District Office, Zhabei Water Patrol Team, Shanghai Municipal Local Produce Trade Association.

Local News Two

Jianghai Customs Seizes Another One Million Yuan Worth of Opium 177

Twenty Loads of Red Soil Shipped from Europe to Dalian

The Smugglers Arrived in Shanghai on a German Ship and are Japanese

The Jianghai Customs has repeatedly reported the seizure of large quantities of heroin. Yesterday morning, from 8:00 a.m. to 10:00 a.m., seven officers from the Jianghai Customs Field Operations Team seized one hundred boxes of opium weighing 19,400 pounds (120 dan) worth one million yuan on the German cargo ship CLAUSE at a wharf next to the China Merchants Bureau's Chinese Warehouse in Pudong. The case was immediately reported to the Customs Commissioner, who ordered the opium to be transported and escorted to the Jianghai Customs Transfer Room for temporary storage and scheduled incineration. The smuggling and discovery of this large quantity of opium were quite tortuous, and it can be inferred from the seized confidential letters that the smuggling operation was large-scale and long-term, with considerable profits. The German cargo ship CLAUSE came from Europe, with Shanghai as its final destination in the Far East. In addition to the seized 120 dan of opium, it also carried a large number of other goods. The shipowner originally planned to unload all the goods and store them in warehouses. The Customs Field Operations Team immediately inspected them in accordance with regulations and found that the number of goods did not match the manifest. There were one hundred boxes of goods not listed on the manifest. At that time, the customs officers did not know that the one hundred boxes of goods were opium worth one million yuan. After inspection, it was discovered that a large quantity of opium had been smuggled into Shanghai. The Customs Commissioner was notified and questioned the shipowner. The shipowner then submitted a confidential letter related to the opium to the Customs Commissioner. After studying the phrases in the letter, it was learned that the smugglers were Japanese and that the opium came from Europe. The letter instructed that it be shipped to Dalian and then transferred to Guangdong, only with the name OLD SMOKER, and no real name specified. It was secretly transported to Shanghai by a German ship and planned to be transferred to a ship for smuggling to Dalian. Unexpectedly, it was seized in Pudong yesterday morning. It can be said that the net of heaven is wide, though its mesh is coarse, it lets nothing through.

The Xin Case Support Association Held an Important Meeting Yesterday 178

The Xin Dingxiang Incident Support Association, formed by local organizations, labor unions, and hometown associations, held an important meeting at the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m. Representatives from the Postal Workers' Union, the French Water and Electricity Workers' Union, the Seamen's Union, the Commercial Workers' Union, the Sino-Foreign Textile Workers' Union, the British-American Tobacco Factory Workers' Union, the Citizens' Federation, the British Shanghai Fire Brigade Workers' Union, the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union, the Steamship Timber Workers' Union, and the Shanghai Hometown Associations of various regions, including Qian Liqun, Mu Zixiang, Zhang Shenzhi, and Zhao Kuiyi from the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association, and dozens of others were present. Mu Zixiang was elected chairman and presided over the meeting. The chairman first reported that the Xin case occurred 36 days ago and has been actively assisted by various organizations. It has been reported that the French Consul sent a letter to the Municipal Government stating that the French sailors who caused the incident have been severely punished, but there has been no news of how they were punished. In the French Consul's letter, we know that the murderer who drowned Xin Dingxiang has been identified and there is now a correct basis in law. We should actively support it as a diplomatic backing to achieve the final victory. The results of the investigation of the Xin case by Ningbo lawyers were reported. It was then resolved: (1) Secret (2) To submit a serious protest to the French authorities through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The Ningbo Fellow Association will draft the petition. (3) Omitted (4) To publish a special issue on the Xin case, organized by Comrade Cheng Zhiliang (5) All labor unions should continue to issue declarations automatically (6) To ask various newspapers and opinion organizations to publish more articles on the Xin case and expand publicity. Other matters are secret and the petition to the Municipal Government and the Ningbo lawyers' investigation report are recorded below:

The Xin Case Support Association's Petition to the Municipal Government: Regarding the case of Sampan rower Xin Dingxiang being brutally beaten and thrown into the river by sailors of the French warship Valdek-Shah after demanding payment for crossing the river to Pudong, we request that you make serious representations to the French authorities based on reason to uphold national dignity and protect the lives of the people. Imperialists rely on unequal treaties as a talisman to exercise gunboat diplomacy, arbitrarily infringe on our sovereignty, insult our national dignity, and massacre our people. Tragic cases occur one after another. In particular, the occurrence of the Xin case has caused public sentiment to be very resentful. However, the French authorities still have no sincerity in resolving it. According to reports, Consul General Gange Lin has replied to your government, stating that the perpetrators have been severely punished by the French Navy and that all losses to the family of the deceased will be compensated. Although the French authorities have stated that they have severely detained the perpetrators, they have not announced which sailor was punished, what his name is, or which article of the country's law was used for the punishment. Our association believes that without the strength of the government and the support of the people to make a serious representation to the French authorities, it will be difficult to appease public anger and achieve the purpose. Therefore, the fourth standing committee meeting of our association resolved to have eight demands for fundamental and symptomatic treatment. In addition to submitting the fundamental demands directly to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the symptomatic demands are: (1) The French authorities should formally apologize to our government and guarantee that similar incidents will not occur in the future (2) Punish the original murderer (3) Compensate Xin Dingxiang's family with 100,000 taels of silver for living expenses (4) Provide Xin Dingxiang with 30,000 taels of silver for funeral expenses. We urge you to take the spirit of the revolution and make serious representations to the French authorities with ten conditions to achieve the purpose of maintaining national dignity and preventing future troubles. We are extremely anxious and await your orders. Sincerely, Xin Dingxiang Incident Support Association of All Circles in Shanghai, respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government.

Ningbo Lawyers' Investigation Report: After investigating the facts of this case, the undersigned convened a meeting at the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association on November 2 this year to question Zhu Gensheng, Ge Amao, and Xin Hesheng, the father of the deceased, who witnessed the incident. They claimed that at 6:05 a.m. on October 16 this year, two French sailors whose names were unknown took rickshaws to the Weituoma Road wharf and took Xin Dingxiang's Sampan to the French "Nasha" (transliteration) merchant ship. They did not pay the fare and went on board the ship. Xin Dingxiang waited beside the ship. At about 7:00 a.m., the two sailors and three sailors from the merchant ship came down the ladder. The three sailors went first, followed by the two sailors. The three sailors crossed Xin Dingxiang's Sampan to Ge Amao's Sampan chartered by the French Far East Shipping Company. One of the sailors immediately followed, and another sailor also wanted to cross over. At that time, Xin Dingxiang stood at the bow of his boat and urgently asked him for the fare. Unexpectedly, he angered the sailor, who punched and kicked him, pushing Xin Dingxiang into the river. At the same time, Sampan rower Zhu Gensheng, who was moored next to the Nasha ship, witnessed this situation and tried to rescue him, but after waiting for half an hour, he did not see Xin Dingxiang float up and had to return his Sampan to the wharf. The three sailors and one sailor in Ge Amao's Sampan saw Xin Dingxiang being beaten and pushed into the river by their companion and feared being implicated if they went ashore, so they asked Ge Amao to row back to the Nasha ship. Ge Amao was rowing the boat when Xin Dingxiang was being beaten by the sailor, so he was facing away from Xin's boat, but he heard the sound and when he turned around, he did not see Dingxiang, knowing that a disaster had occurred. After the sailors boarded the ship, he saw that Dingxiang's Sampan was still floating, so he took the Sampan and tied it to a barge and reported it to his father, Xin Hesheng. Xin Hesheng was shocked to hear the news and went to the Weituoma Road wharf to inquire. At that time, the two sailors were trying to avoid disaster and hired another Sampan to row to the Xiantuoma Road wharf, intending to escape. One sailor saw a group of boatmen standing and waiting on the wharf and, fearing that there would be trouble, jumped ashore before the boat docked. The boatmen bravely stepped forward and subdued him. The sailor dared to strike wildly with his belt. Fortunately, the crowd ignored the danger and firmly subdued him. The 415 Indian police patrol arrived and handed him over to the Indian police, who transferred him to the police station, but he was privately released. Another sailor fell behind and was also subdued by the boatmen and sent to the water police station. After questioning the witness Ge Amao and others, the sailor was still privately released and a small steamship was sent to escort him to the Huishan wharf to disembark. On October 21, Xin Dingxiang's body floated to the surface. The prosecutor of the Shanghai Local Court verified that he had drowned to death during his lifetime. The French Concession Lujiawan police station summoned Xin Hesheng twice on October 24 and 28, demanding a settlement. The first time, a Western police officer gave him one hundred yuan, but he refused to accept it, saying that he had to ask his daughter-in-law. The water police station also summoned Xin Hesheng on October 30. A Western police officer's words contained intimidation. These facts were jointly investigated by the undersigned. Two French sailors should have paid Xin Dingxiang the fare, but they refused to pay it first. Xin Dingxiang stood at the bow of the Sampan. If he was pushed, there was a clear possibility of drowning. Anyone could recognize the danger of the outcome. The French sailor pushed him recklessly, causing Xin Dingxiang to drown and die. His actions are suspected of intentional homicide. As for the 415 Indian police and the water police station arbitrarily releasing the above-mentioned French sailors suspected of homicide without directly prosecuting them according to law, they are also suspected of dereliction of duty. The matter concerns national rights and the lives of the people. We dare to report the results of our investigation. Investigators: Lawyers Wei Jiong, Dai Chengxiang, Hu Feng, Lian Hu Xilian, Chen Zijuan, Liu Cailiang, Zhang Henghai, Zhou Hui, Yu Hualong, Hu Yongde, Wang Jianfan, Yuan Jiahong, Dai Jinghuai, Feng Kan.

Sea Bandits Fight Fiercely Outside the Wusong Estuary 179

Bandit Ships Everywhere on the Sea

Merchant Ships and Boats are Robbed

Pan Kaiwu, the leader of the sea bandits, and Shen Gongxi, another leader of the sea bandits, engaged in internal strife and failed to reach a peace agreement in the waters off Wusong Estuary, Fengli, and Juegang, resulting in mutual attacks. Details have been reported in this newspaper. According to yesterday's news, after two fierce artillery battles between Pan and Shen, both sides suffered significant losses. However, because the strength of the two gangs of sea bandits is similar, neither side has retreated. In the past two or three days, the situation has escalated from positional warfare to mixed warfare. After Shen Guanxi's gang of sea bandits was driven back from Shayugang by Pan's gang, they learned that Pan's gang's base camp, Lvsi Sanjia Town, had been emptied of bandits and was weak. Therefore, Shen Guanshou led the bandit ships to resist Pan's bandits on one side, while Shen Guanxi personally led more than 40 bandit ships to the outer sea. They sailed to the Lvsi sea area the day before yesterday and intercepted Pan's gang. They were completely unprepared and suffered heavy casualties. The Shen bandits occupied Pengjia Tao in that sea area and seized more than ten bandit ships from Pan's side. More than one hundred defeated bandits from Pan's gang planned to escape back to Sanjia Town, but were blocked by patrol boats from the Fourth District and Eighteenth Team of the Wusong Waterborne Provincial Public Security Team and the Nantong County Public Security Team. Because the base camp had been lost, they scattered. At the same time, the Shen bandits in the Juegang and Fengli sea areas were attacked by Pan's gang and suffered significant losses. There was also news that Shen Guan had been killed by Pan's bandits. Later, Pan's gang heard that the base camp had been lost and immediately led dozens of bandit ships back to fight Shen's bandits fiercely. According to the situation a few days ago, almost every sea area outside the Wusong Estuary was occupied by sea bandits, and the chaos was extreme. Most of the merchant ships entering and leaving the port were robbed. The ships that reported incidents at the port in the past two days included the Ningbo Liu Gang ship Zhao Xiangxing, the sand barge Xin Deli, Chen Shunxing, Yang Taimao, Jin Yongxing, Jin Baoxing, Ni Shunmao, and others. There were still many unreported. Therefore, most of the sand fishing boats for export, seeing the danger of navigation, did not dare to sail alone. The Wusong Water Police's 17th and 18th teams have dispatched Zhenhai and Qinghai gunboats to sweep the waters outside the port.

Joint Trial of Zhao Case Murderers, 180

Questioning of Ji and Xia

Vigorous Arrests of Fugitives Still in Progress

The assassination of Zhao Tieqiao, General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau in Shanghai, by thugs, has been repeatedly ordered by various agencies, and rewards have been offered for their arrest. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Detective Team managed to obtain clues and, after many investigations, arrested the main culprit, Wang Jinshan, also known as Wang Ganting, nicknamed Wang Xiaolaosan. Wang Jinshan confessed that in a certain month, he was instructed by someone to open a room on the second floor of the Dalu Hotel in the French Concession to secretly plan an assassination, inviting accomplices to participate. At the time, he distributed box guns and six-round revolvers to Xia Guangyao (i.e., Xia Shaoen) and three others, who went to the entrance of the China Merchants Bureau to wait for Zhao's car to arrive. Xia Guangyao and others simultaneously opened fire, hitting Zhao, causing his death. Afterward, he received one thousand yuan, which he distributed to the others, and recovered the firearms. Recently, Director Shen of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau followed a lead to Xiajiacun in Hefei County, Anhui Province, and arrested Xia Shaoen and escorted him back to Shanghai. On the morning of the 19th of this month, Director Shen of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau personally brought the arrested Xia Shaoen to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau to confront Wang Jinshan in court. Xia Shaoen confessed that he was invited by Wang Jinshan to a certain place in the French Concession to plan the assassination. At the time, Wang Jinshan issued him a six-round revolver. Wang Jinshan also carried a handgun and rode a bicycle to guide him and three others to the entrance of the China Merchants Bureau to wait for Zhao to get out of the car and opened fire to assassinate him. Afterward, Wang Jinshan gave him one hundred yuan and recovered the handgun. He admitted to the charges. Wang Jinshan's confession confirmed the details. The investigation revealed that there were four accomplices in this case. Wang Jinshan, the principal culprit who conspired, incited, and directed the assassination, and Xia Shaoen, the main culprit who opened fire, have been successively arrested and interrogated. It has been verified that Xia Shaoen was carrying a six-round revolver, which is consistent with the hospital's examination that Zhao was shot with a lead bullet. The facts of the case are clear. The authorities are urging a thorough and strict investigation of the remaining fugitives, and it is believed that the remaining fugitives will soon be arrested.

Another Telegram of Support for the Xiao Case 182

Telegram from Qiaolianhui (Overseas Chinese Federation) et al. to the Fujian Provincial Government

Regarding the Xiamen Authorities Prohibiting the Arrival of Java Steamships

The Overseas Chinese Federation, Overseas Chinese Affairs Promotion Association, Seamen's General Union, Shanghai Women's Association, and other groups yesterday telegraphed to Chairman Yang and all members of the Fujian Provincial Government, stating: "Reports state that the Xiamen Garrison Commander has presented a request approved by the Provincial Government to suppress (boycott Java steamships). Based on your government's usual words and deeds, our association and others deeply believe that the reports are inaccurate. The current anti-Dutch movement was sparked by the defilement of female teacher Xiao Xin'an, which stems from the abuse of our overseas Chinese compatriots over the years. During the early Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty, Dutch soldiers cruelly massacred over ten thousand overseas Chinese. The Manchu rulers, intent on suppressing the Han, sat idly by without intervening, allowing the Dutch to become increasingly reckless. Throughout the Qing Dynasty, countless innocent overseas Chinese were killed. Since the Republic of China era, in various ports such as (Lassen), (Yingli), (Jukang), (Shengwa), (Wentongan), (Ganmenghua), (Gudusi), (Taiyang), (Wanlidong), and (Sanfapo), overseas Chinese have either been harmed by indigenous people or massacred by Dutch soldiers. Not a single life has been vindicated, and not a single case has been compensated. Conversely, the Dutch in our country are always protected by local officials, and any bullying or harassment must be severely punished according to the law. Why are others valued while we are demeaned? Anyone with nationalistic sentiments cannot but feel deeply resentful. But it is a heavenly principle that all humans are equal, while the Dutch despise the Chinese. Article 109 of the regulations in the Dutch colonies clearly stipulates that Chinese people are an inferior race, classified with local indigenous people, Arabs, Africans, Muslims, or polytheists, and are governed by special inferior laws. Japanese and all Europeans are a superior race, classified with the Dutch and receiving special respect from the Dutch government. In social interactions and prison treatment, Chinese people are not equal to Westerners. Even your esteemed persons, whom our association and others respect, and other military and political leaders are regarded as an inferior race in the eyes of the Dutch because Article 109 of the Dutch colonial regulations does not have a provision stating (but Chinese military and political authorities are not subject to this). The entire area of the Netherlands is only over twelve thousand square miles, less than three percent of our country. The population is only over five million, about 1.4 percent of our country. They are not worthy of being imperialists. However, the Dutch are peaceful and submissive towards Japan, while they are cruel and arrogant towards China. They especially regard our KMT (Nationalist Party), which saves the world and the country, as enemies. During the late Qing Dynasty, Qiu Xiating of Batavia secretly invited our Premier to Batavia, but the Dutch refused to allow him to disembark. This is what our Premier regretted the most, and what our party members should forever remember. The Northern Expedition of the righteous army unified the country, and our international status should have increased. However, the Dutch have intensified their contempt for our party and oppression. Schools are not allowed to hang the Premier's portrait, students are not allowed to read the Three Principles of the People textbooks, and no memorial weeks for the Premier can be held in any organizations. Documents and communications are not allowed to contain the phrases (Down with Imperialism) and (Abolish Unequal Treaties). Those who do not comply, whether they are executive committee members, supervisors, principals, or teachers, are arbitrarily detained and immediately deported. The Premier is the Premier of our country, the schools are the schools of our country, and the students are the students of our country. Why should they overstep their bounds and interfere? Their intentions are even more malicious than burning books and burying scholars. If we were to imitate them, how could foreigners tolerate it? The Dutch East Indies used to be subordinate to our country. Overseas Chinese have migrated there for over a thousand years, with over three million people residing there. When our people first went to the Dutch East Indies, there was no so-called entry tax. The entry tax was first levied in the first year of the Republic of China (1912) at twenty-five guilders per person. Then, due to successful collection, it was increased to fifty guilders. Since there was seemingly no protest, it was increased again to one hundred guilders. It is estimated that since the tax was first levied, overseas Chinese have paid approximately ten million yuan in this tax. Last year, the Dutch colonial council resolved to increase it again to one hundred and fifty guilders from July 1929. Lin Youren and other citizens residing in Beijing petitioned the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to protest, which resulted in a delay. In June of this year, the colonial council revived the old case and resolved to implement the increase of the entry tax to one hundred and fifty guilders per person from 1931. They also intend to retroactively collect an entry tax of seventy-five guilders per person for indentured laborers who have been tragically lured and sold. Conversely, those from the Dutch colonies who come to China are not charged a single cent. We treat the Dutch as the most favored nation, while they treat us as the lowest nation. How can we not feel resentful at such an act of repaying kindness with evil? Dutch officials of all ranks deliberately mistreat overseas Chinese. They arbitrarily levy taxes and abuse punishments on those who have already entered the country. Those who have just arrived at the port are often first detained in detention centers, and old customers are not allowed to provide legal guarantees at any time. Friends and relatives are not allowed to visit, and food is not allowed to be sent in, leaving them without food all day and without sleep all night. Since they cannot communicate in the language, they also lose their freedom of urination and defecation. Many weak women and children become ill and die as a result. The treatment is more severe than that of criminals. The strictness of the search leaves no one untouched, even women. Conversely, Japanese or Europeans arriving on the same ship are leisurely and comfortable, with no difficulty. Compared to this, how can we endure it? This accumulation of evil has aroused public outrage. Our association and others have invited various sectors to jointly launch a support Xiao and anti-Dutch conference. Those who have agreed to participate include the Chinese Vocational Education Society, Labor University, Lawyers Association, and over ten legal entities. The local municipal party headquarters has also replied with approval and will expand publicity through party organizations at all levels. The conference will declare support and various sectors will celebrate the Premier's birthday memorial. We are sending a telegram to the government requesting serious negotiations. The people's hearts are not dead, and the national spirit can be revived. As for anti-Dutch methods, boycotting the Java Steamship Company is the most effective. First, because the crew members of the company are the culprits who insult our nation. Without punishment, we cannot be human. Second, the decline of the company can attract the attention of the Dutch government, and the suffering of overseas Chinese can hopefully be improved. If we were to strike at the boycott movement, it would be tantamount to handing a weapon to the enemy and harming ourselves. The result of self-harm would harm the entire country, especially the people of Fujian. About two million overseas Chinese in the Dutch colonies are from Fujian, and over ten thousand Fujianese overseas Chinese travel on Java steamships every year. Second, Xiao Xin'an must be a young lady from Fujian. Therefore, we urgently request your Excellency, for the sake of the party, the country, overseas Chinese, and our hometown, to immediately order Commander Lin of Xiamen to retract the order (suppressing the boycott of Java steamships) and to dismiss the magistrate of Siming County, who recklessly requested the suppression of the enemy movement. The people of the entire country will sing your praises without end. This pressing petition is presented with utmost trepidation, awaiting your command. Overseas Chinese Federation, Overseas Chinese Affairs Promotion Association, Seamen's General Union, Shanghai Women's Association, Taiwan Chinese General Hall, Shanghai Academy, Fujian Society, Yixing Society, Yixing Fellow Townsmen Support Group in Shanghai, respectfully bowing in unison."

Public Works Bureau Patrol Boat Rescues Cargo Ship in Huangpu River 183

Preserving Cargo Worth Ten Thousand Gold

At around 11:00 AM on the 18th, a Songjiang-bound boat (owned by Xue Yuesheng), bearing the license plate number 712335 for cargo ships in Shanghai, was fully loaded with general merchandise worth over ten thousand gold, heading from Shanghai to Songjiang. As it passed behind the Dongjiadu Wharf of the Dalae Company, a steamship sped by and failed to avoid it, resulting in a violent collision. The sound was heard by Gao Chao, an employee of the Public Works Bureau's Shipping Department at Dongjiadu. He immediately dispatched patrol boat number one, along with police officer Lou Tingyao and others, to provide assistance. By then, the Dalae steamship had already sailed far away. The cargo ship had a large hole in the rear hold on the left side, and water had already entered, causing it to sink. Small boats surrounded the ship, frantically grabbing cargo. Gao saw that the ship was stranded in the river and unable to dock on its own. He immediately ordered the boats to return the items they had taken and used the patrol boat to tow the ship to the Dongjiadu Wharf. Fortunately, the wind and waves were not strong, and both the people and the goods were preserved. It is said that in addition to employee Gao, police officer Lou Tingyao, the patrol boat captain, stoker, and sailors also contributed greatly. The bureau has already conveyed its praise to them.

Yu Henian Attempts Suicide in Suzhou 191

Rescued Early, Likely to Recover

Yu Henian, a 25-year-old Wuxi native who previously worked at the Nanhua Printing Company at 7 Taopeng Road, opposite the Ewo Cotton Mill in Yangshupu, quit his job in September. Unable to return to his hometown, he stayed in Shanghai and spent all his money on food and lodging. Feeling unable to face his elders in his hometown, he became despondent and secretly bought a bottle of sleeping pills from a pharmacy, fearing that committing suicide in Shanghai would be a laughingstock to his friends. The day before yesterday, he took a train to Suzhou and stayed at a room in the First Inn outside Changmen. On the day of his arrival in Suzhou, he spent the whole day sightseeing and returned to the inn in the evening. After dinner, he closed the door tightly and wrote two suicide notes, one to his parents, stating that he should not have drifted around, which led to his unemployment and made him unable to return home, and the other to the inn's accounting office, detailing his origin and requesting that his father (named Yu Huizhong) be notified to collect his body in Suzhou. After writing the letters, he swallowed all the sleeping pills and went to bed. At 10:00 AM the next morning, the inn's tea house worker entered the room after Yu did not wake up and found him lying stiffly on the bed, his expression pale. Knowing that he had taken poison, he saw an empty bottle of sleeping pills and two suicide notes on the bed. He immediately notified the accounting office, who sent him to Suzhou Yong Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, he had taken only a small amount of poison and his life could be saved. The inn has sent a letter to Yu's father, Huizhong, in Wuxi to come to Suzhou and handle the matter, and has also sent a letter to the Nanhua Company to inquire about everything.

Woman Sues Father for Obstructing Marriage Engagement 192

Plaintiff's Lawsuit Dismissed

Ji Gengxiong, a woman from Yancheng, engaged lawyer Zhang Enzhi to file a lawsuit in the local court, requesting marital autonomy. The lawsuit stated that her father (the defendant), Ji Xianzhi, was obstructing her marriage engagement. A man surnamed Zhou from the same hometown, who is currently widowed, proposed marriage to the plaintiff. However, the defendant adamantly obstructed this marriage. The plaintiff has reached the legal age of majority, and her marriage should be autonomous, as permitted by current law. The defendant, Ji Xianzhi, also engaged lawyers Zhang Guohua and Ren Enji to file a defense. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao Zhenhai opened the court for trial. The plaintiff, Ji Gengxiong, 23 years old, from Yancheng and residing at 68 Shajia Street, Lujiabang Road, testified about the events. (Question) Is the defendant your father? (Answer) Yes. (Question) Whom do you want to marry? (Answer) I want to marry a man surnamed Zhou. (Question) Did you discuss it with your father? (Answer) My father did not agree. The defendant, Ji Xianzhi, 46 years old, residing on a boat in Shenjia Garden, testified. (Question) How old is your daughter? (Answer) Nineteen years old, born on October 16th. (Question) Why do you not allow your daughter to marry Zhou? (Answer) Because Zhou does not have a proper job. (Question) Whom do you want your daughter to marry? (Answer) I want her to marry someone surnamed Hu from our hometown. (Question) Did you discuss it with your daughter? (Answer) Yes, I did. I really hope my daughter will change her mind. At this point, the lawyers for both sides argued. Judge Zhao announced, "The court renders its judgment in this case. The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed." The reasons for the judgment will be recorded. Marriages must be agreed upon by both the father and the daughter. After the two sides signed the judgment, the court adjourned.

Flour Ship Sinks in the Huangpu River 194

Losses Exceed Three Thousand Yuan

Yesterday, the Tongshunchang Customs Brokerage on Rue de la Porte de l'Ouest hired a wharf boat owned by Cai Songlin to transport 1,500 bags of flour to the North China Steamboat Company's pier near Buoy Nos. 2 and 3 of the South Huangpu Customs for unloading. At 11:30 AM, the tide rose rapidly, and the mooring rope of the boat suddenly broke. The boat drifted southward and was quickly capsized by the waves. All the flour on board sank into the Huangpu River. The loss is estimated to be over three thousand yuan, as each bag of flour is valued at three yuan and two jiao.

Selling Stamps on the Street 195

Elementary School Teacher Driven to Desperation

Arrested by Police Detective

Huang Jing, a native of Chongming who works as a teacher at an elementary school, came to Shanghai from his hometown to visit friends, but was unsuccessful. Having spent all his money, he was in dire straits. Yesterday afternoon, he was selling twenty-one one-jiao stamps in front of the General Post Office on North Sichuan Road to people mailing letters. A crowd gathered to watch. Detective Shen Dehui of the Hongkou Police Station saw this and arrested Huang for violating police regulations, taking him and the stamps to the police station. The police chief briefly questioned him and ordered him to be detained and sent to the court for questioning.

Fire on Rue Massenet Last Night 196

At 6:35 PM last night, thick smoke suddenly billowed from the upper floor of the Shunji Tailor Shop at 251 Rue Massenet in the French Concession, enveloping the surrounding area. The police officers on duty nearby noticed the smoke and immediately reported it to the fire department by phone. The Grand Sentry Bell and the Montigny Road Fire Brigade arrived at the scene one after another. By the time they arrived, the fire had already been extinguished by nearby residents. It is said that the fire was caused by smoldering cigarette butts accidentally thrown into cotton wadding.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Preservation of Incense and Candle Industry 199

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a letter to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday, stating: "Regarding the request for consideration, we received a letter from the Incense and Candle Trade Association on the 19th, stating that they read a report on the 11th that the city's party and government authorities had resolved to promote the national calendar and to confiscate and fine shop owners, managers, and residents who sell goods such as incense, candles, and paper horses for Lunar New Year celebrations. The association pointed out that while the authorities' move to promote the national calendar is well-intentioned, the Lunar New Year falls at the end of February on the national calendar, close to Qingming Festival, when people typically purchase incense and candles to worship their ancestors. If the municipal authorities use the sale of these items as the standard for confiscation and punishment, people who purchase incense and candles to commemorate their ancestors may be mistakenly identified as celebrating the Lunar New Year. Police officers with clear orders will be able to interfere at will, and merchants will be unable to defend themselves, leading to financial losses and imprisonment. The sale of incense and candles will be greatly affected, and the livelihoods of tens of thousands of businesses will be threatened. Therefore, the association members unanimously requested a meeting to discuss ways to address the situation. It was resolved to actively inform the public to comply with the national calendar and to request that the municipal authorities instruct their departments to be lenient and make distinctions regarding citizens purchasing incense and candles for ancestor worship in February, so that they would not be wrongly accused of superstitious practices. The association members also pointed out that incense and candles are used for weddings, birthdays, memorials, and other occasions, and not just for Lunar New Year celebrations. Prohibiting the sale of these items during the entire month of the Lunar New Year would not only disrupt legitimate uses, but would also be equivalent to forcing incense and candle shops to close for the entire month, leading to significant losses. The association respectfully requests that your bureau review the situation and take appropriate action to benefit the public. Sincerely submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs."

Extension of the Deadline for Amending Patent Medicine Package Inserts 200

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a letter to the New Medicine Trade Association, relaying a directive from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, approving a request from the Ministry of Health regarding the investigation and handling of cases related to the "Regulations for the Management of Patent Medicines." These regulations were promulgated and implemented on April 26th of this year and were separately communicated to various provinces and cities for compliance. Numerous drug merchants have reported that Article 5 of the regulations stipulates that various patent medicines sold before the implementation of these regulations must, within six months of their implementation, apply for re-inspection and obtain permits in accordance with Article 2. However, the procedures for amending drug package inserts, prescriptions, and printed materials are complex and time-consuming, making it impossible to complete them in a timely manner, and they requested an extension of the deadline. After careful verification by the Ministry, these claims were found to be valid. To address the difficulties faced by the merchants, it was approved that the original deadline in Article 5 of the regulations be extended for another six months, until April 26th, 1931, as a gesture of consideration. A report has been submitted and separate communications have been sent for review and instructions to ensure uniform compliance by all relevant parties.

Failure of Negotiations in the Labor Strike at the British American Tobacco Factory 204

Workers in the tinfoil section of the new British American Tobacco Company factory in Pudong went on strike on the 18th to protest the factory's unwarranted dismissal of twenty workers and the assault of worker No. 89 by foreman Pope, as well as the expulsion of other workers. Despite several rounds of negotiations between labor and management, the labor side demanded that the management pay severance pay to the dismissed workers, equivalent to six months' salary per worker, and dismiss foreman Pope. However, the factory authorities took a firm stance, resulting in no resolution. It is now learned that yesterday, Zhou Funong from the Municipal Party Headquarters and Wang Gang from the Social Affairs Bureau, along with labor union representatives Chen Peide, Gu Ruobe, Li Guangxian, and others, re-entered the factory for negotiations, indicating that the labor side had made concessions. Their demands were reduced to three: (1) Severance pay for the dismissed workers should be based on their years of service, with one month's salary for each year of service as the standard, and proportionally more for longer service. (2) Double the savings funds should be issued. (3) Foreman Pope should be dismissed. The factory did not agree to the above three demands, resulting in no resolution, and the negotiations broke down. Last night, the workers in that section gathered at the union to hold a meeting and resolved not to resume work until their demands were met and to appeal to higher authorities for a fair resolution.

The Eating Habits of University Students 210

— Xiao Lu

Indeed, university students are "big" in everything—their knowledge, expenses, and even their eating habits. How can we prove this? We can use the eateries in front of the university gates as evidence.

Almost every university has a consumer cooperative, which naturally sells mostly food items. However, this is not enough; they also need external eateries to supplement their food supply. Their eating habits can also be divided into seasons—generally hot in winter and cold in summer, with no standard in spring and autumn. Confectionery is suitable for all seasons.

Regarding the price of food, it goes without saying that it is expensive. A medium-quality meal package costs eleven and a half yuan per month (for only two meals). A single pear or orange costs more than ten cents. On average, each person eats six times a day. The first time is breakfast, the second time is a snack at 10:00 AM, the third time is lunch, the fourth time is a snack at 4:00 PM, the fifth time is dinner, and the sixth time is a snack at 10:00 PM. This does not include fruits after lunch and dinner, and large dishes on Saturdays or Sundays.

In this way, expenses naturally increase greatly. It is truly too difficult when there is no money. If they don't eat, they can't get by, but if they eat, they have no money. Therefore, they come up with the ingenious method of keeping accounts. Small vendors are also very welcome because keeping accounts can increase business. By the end of the season, each person has to pay at least twenty or thirty yuan in account money.

There are also a few clever ones who have come up with a [method of free-loading]. This free-loading is not free-loading from classmates, but free-loading from the eateries. It is difficult to free-load from external eateries; the easiest is to free-load from the consumer cooperative because the consumer cooperative is run by the student union. How is this free-loading done? Most of the time, it involves not repaying the account or only repaying half of it. By the time the student union is reorganized the following year, the president has changed, and the old accounts are forgotten, so the free-loading is successful.

The consumer cooperative of C University, because there were too many people free-loading, came up with an ingenious method of [limiting the collection of accounts to certain dates and having the training department collect the unpaid accounts]. The training department is meant to train students, and students who do such immoral things naturally want to train him.

There are also a few even cleverer ones who think that keeping accounts is unstable and may still be collected, so they don't even keep accounts, free-loading openly. Recently, the consumer cooperative of C University posted a notice that reads:

[Mr. So-and-so, you often grace our cooperative at 9:00 AM, eating for free. We should announce your name, but we are temporarily keeping it secret out of consideration. We hope you will be cautious in the future.]

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 211

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc. are included in the introduction. However, frivolous books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to the latest works of new artists at home and abroad and accompanying illustrations related to the text.

(3) Verifications or researches of ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) Each text should not exceed 3,000 words at most.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, and do not write in cursive script. Western writing should be abbreviated if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(8) Do not draw pictures with blue ink and do not use colored paper. White paper and black drawings are required.

(9) Please indicate that the manuscript is collected by the Book and Newspaper Introduction Editing Department.
